"[vim]<br><br><img src=""Screenshot 2025-03-13 at 11.59.41.png""><br><br>Delete this entire function.<br><br>Start by moving the cursor to function h_prompt.<br><br>Then after the cursor is sitting at the start of the function, use another command to delete everything from the cursor to the end of the function."	"1. <b>/function h_prompt</b>, then <b>enter</b> <br>to get to the function.<br><br>2. Then type <b>d/^end$</b>, which will delete everything up to the word ""end"".<br><br><u><i>If you want to also delete the word end:</i></u><br><br><b>d/^end$/e</b> <br>(e stands for ""end of match"")"
"[vim]<br><br>use visual mode to delete the following:<br><br>function h_prompt<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; set_color cyan&nbsp; # Username in cyan<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; echo -n (whoami)<br><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; set_color normal<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; echo -n ""@""<br><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; set_color blue&nbsp; # Hostname in blue<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; echo -n (hostname | cut -d . -f1)&nbsp; # Short hostname<br><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; set_color normal<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; echo -n "" ""<br><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; set_color yellow&nbsp; # Last two directories in yellow<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; echo -n (string join ""/"" (string split ""/"" (pwd) | tail -n 2))<br><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; set_color normal<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; echo -n "" % ""<br>end"	`/function h_prompt` to get to the first line.<br><br>enter visual line mode: V<br><br>/^end$/ to get to the last line.<br><br>Press d to delete
"[vim]<br><br>delete everything by deleting the function plus the following line<br><br>function h_prompt<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; set_color cyan&nbsp; # Username in cyan<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; echo -n (whoami)<br><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; set_color normal<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; echo -n ""@""<br><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; set_color blue&nbsp; # Hostname in blue<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; echo -n (hostname | cut -d . -f1)&nbsp; # Short hostname<br><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; set_color normal<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; echo -n "" ""<br><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; set_color yellow&nbsp; # Last two directories in yellow<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; echo -n (string join ""/"" (string split ""/"" (pwd) | tail -n 2))<br><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; set_color normal<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; echo -n "" % ""<br>end<br>test<br><br><b>Hint:</b><br>Start with d/"	"Starting at the top line (function h_prompt), type: <br>d/^end$/+1d<br><br>- this deletes everything, plus the next line containing ""test"""
[vim]<br><br>delete all functions of the following format:<br><br>function my_func<br>end<br><br>Use :g/	:g/^function /,/^end$/d
"[vim]<br><br>Delete the following function using `:` and a comma, in a single line.<br><br>function h_prompt<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; set_color cyan&nbsp; # Username in cyan<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; echo -n (whoami)<br><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; set_color normal<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; echo -n ""@""<br><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; set_color blue&nbsp; # Hostname in blue<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; echo -n (hostname | cut -d . -f1)&nbsp; # Short hostname<br><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; set_color normal<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; echo -n "" ""<br><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; set_color yellow&nbsp; # Last two directories in yellow<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; echo -n (string join ""/"" (string split ""/"" (pwd) | tail -n 2))<br><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; set_color normal<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; echo -n "" % ""<br>end"	":/function h_prompt/,/^end$/d<br><br>/function h_prompt/ looks for the first occurence of ""function h_prompt""<br><br>/^end$/ looks for a line containing only ""end""<br><br>/d deletes everything in between these two matches (inclusive)"

"[tech]<br>[vscode] [containers]<br><br>In a VSCode Dev Container, why might this postCreateCommand be needed?<br><br>""postCreateCommand"": ""sudo chown -R node:node /app/node_modules && npm install"""	This command fixes permissions issues with node_modules, especially when the folder was created by root (e.g. during Docker image build).<br><br>sudo chown -R node:node /app/node_modules:<br>Recursively changes ownership of the node_modules directory to the node user inside the container.<br><br>npm install:<br>Installs dependencies as the node user, preventing permission errors.<br><br><br>This is often needed because:<br><br>Dockerfile steps run as root by default.<br><br>The VSCode Dev Container often uses the node user for non-root operations.<br><br>Without this fix, npm install can fail with EACCES or permission denied error.<br>

docker compose build --no-cache<br><div>VS</div><div>docker compose build</div>	"<div><div><div>When you run `docker compose build --no-cache`</div></div><div><br></div><div>Youre telling Docker to:</div><br><div><br></div><br><blockquote> <b>Ignore all previously cached layers</b> and <b>rebuild everything from scratch</b>, even if nothing has changed in your files.</blockquote><br><div></div><br><div><b> Normally, Docker caching works like this:</b><b></b></div><br><div><br></div><br><div>When building an image from a Dockerfile, Docker caches <b>each layer</b>, for example:</div></div><div><br></div><div><img src=""CleanShot 2025-03-25 at 14.43.37@2x.png""><br></div><div><br></div><div>If the package.json hasnt changed, Docker <b>reuses</b> the cached npm install step  making builds much faster.</div><br><div></div><br><div><b> But when you use --no-cache:</b><b></b></div><br><div><br></div><br><div>Docker <b>ignores all that</b> and re-runs every instruction:</div><br><div>  Re-downloads base images</div><br><div>  Re-installs dependencies</div><br><div>  Re-copies files</div><br><div>  Re-compiles native modules (like sharp, better-sqlite3, etc.)</div><br><div><br></div><br><div> This is very useful when:</div><br><div>  Youre switching CPU architectures (e.g., ARM  x86)</div><br><div>  You suspect something is broken in a cached layer</div><br><div>  You changed something subtle that Docker didnt detect</div>"

When writing a custom script using eza, fzf, htop why might the formatting be being messed up?<br><br>For example, I was using eza and when I run it in the terminal alone it prints icons and a nice grid layout. When I combined it with other commands in a custom script it was losing all formats.<br><br>Besides the quirks within vscode, what else might be happening?	&nbsp; &nbsp; Programs like eza, ls, fzf, htop, etc. check if stdout is a real terminal<br>&nbsp; &nbsp; Without a real TTY, they disable formatting, color, layout, etc.
What is a tty?	"<div><b>TTY</b> stands for <b>Teletypewriter</b>  originally referring to physical terminals used to communicate with mainframes in the early days of computing.</div>
<div><br></div>
<div>In modern systems, a <b>TTY is any device or interface that acts like a text-based terminal.</b><b></b></div>
<div></div>
<div><h3><b> In Practice:</b></h3></div>
<div><br></div>
<div>A <b>TTY</b> is:</div>
<div><ul><li>
<div>A <b>real or virtual terminal</b> where you can <b>type</b> and <b>see output</b>.</div>
</li><li>
<div>Your <b>Terminal.app</b>, <b>iTerm</b>, <b>GNOME Terminal</b>, or <b>VS Code integrated terminal</b> (sometimes).</div></li></ul></div>"
When using a TTY vs not using a TTY?	<div><h3><b> When a program detects a TTY:</b></h3></div><br><div><ul><li><br><div>It <b>shows colors</b><b></b></div><br></li><li><br><div>It <b>uses grid layouts</b>, <b>interactive UIs</b>, and <b>animations</b><b></b></div><br></li><li><br><div>Think: eza, fzf, htop, less, vim</div><br></li></ul></div><br><div></div><br><div><h3><b> When&nbsp;</b></h3><h3><b>not</b></h3><h3><b>&nbsp;connected to a TTY:</b></h3></div><br><div><ul><li><br><div>Output is redirected (e.g., piped to a file or another command)</div><br></li><li><br><div>The program <b>disables formatting</b> (to avoid polluting logs)</div><br></li><li><br><div>Behavior is often plain, like one item per line or no color</div></li></ul></div>
[tech]<br><br><div><div>vite app</div><div><br></div><div>.env:</div><div>STRAPI_UPLOAD_TOKEN=b7fc3101cab7</div></div><div><br></div><div>{</div><div><div><div>&nbsp; 'Authorization': `Bearer ${import.meta.env.STRAPI_UPLOAD_TOKEN}`</div><div>}</div><div></div></div></div>	This won't work. In VITE, all environment variables must be prefixed with VITE_<br><br>ie<br><br>.env:<br>VITE_STRAPI_UPLOAD_TOKEN=<br><br><div>{</div><div><div><div>&nbsp; 'Authorization': `Bearer ${import.meta.env.VITE_STRAPI_UPLOAD_TOKEN}`</div><div>}</div></div></div>
[bash]<br><br>set -eux<br><br>What is this?	-x (<b>xtrace)&nbsp;</b>prints every command before executing, prefixed with a +<br><br>-e (<b>errexit)&nbsp;</b>exit immediately if any command fails.<br>Otherwise it will keep running.<br><br>-u (<b>no unset)&nbsp;</b>treat unset variables as errors.<br>If we try and access a variable that doesn't exist then it's an error.
[containers]<br><br>Why use `set -eux` ?	Because it prevents containers from being partially built (-e). If a command fails then the layer doesn't get cached as successful.<br><br>-u is set so that if you reference an environment variable you forgot to define , then it fails loudly.<br><br>-x prints each command so that build logs are traceable.
[docker]<br><br>How to make sure build logs are traceable?	use `set -x`
[bash]<br><br>What does the following do?<br><br>set -a	<div>Automatically export <b>all variables</b> defined from now on.</div><div><br></div><div><div>This means anything defined (like FOO=bar) will not only be a shell variable, but also an <b>environment variable</b>, which is important because some tools (like aider) only read env vars.</div></div>
[bash]<br><br>What does the following do?<br><br>set +a	<div>Undoes `set -a`, which automatically will export all defined vars.</div><div><br></div><div>Turns off auto-export mode.<br><br><div>So future variables wont be automatically exported unless you do so manually with export.</div></div>
What does the following do?<br><br>set -a<br>source .env<br>set +a	1. Every variable defined after `set -a` will be automatically exported as an environment variable.<br>&nbsp; i.e. now running `FOO=bar` is like doing `export FOO=bar`<br><br>2. Loads and runs the .env file lin-by-line, defining each var in the current shell.<br>&nbsp; i.e. if my .env file looks like this:<br>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; AIDER_API_KEY=deepseek=sk-abc123<div>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; DEBUG=true</div><div>&nbsp; ..those become <b>exported</b> environment variables.</div><div><br></div><div>3. Return things back to normal by turning off the automatic export mode.</div>

How to disable ACL in strapi?&nbsp;	(example)<br><br>config/plugins.js:<br><br>const awsConfig = {<br>&nbsp; &nbsp; params: {<br>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; ACL: null
"S3 Bucket Policy:<br><br>{<br>&nbsp; ""Version"": ""2012-10-17"",<br>&nbsp; ""Statement"": [<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; {<br>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; [What properties should be in here?]<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; }<br>&nbsp; ]<br>}"	Sid,<br>Effect,<br>Resource<br>Action,<br>Principal 
"<div>S3 Bucket Policy (For my cards system):<br><br>{</div><br><div>&nbsp; ""Version"": ""2012-10-17"",</div><br><div>&nbsp; ""Statement"": [</div><br><div>&nbsp; &nbsp; {</div><br><div>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; ""Sid"": ""[1]"",</div><br><div>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; ""Effect"": ""Allow"",</div><br><div>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; ""Principal"": ""*"",</div><br><div>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; ""Action"": ""[2]"",</div><br><div>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; ""Resource"": ""arn:aws:s3:::luketych_my_bucket_name/*""</div><br><div>&nbsp; &nbsp; }</div><br><div>&nbsp; ]</div><br><div>}</div>"	[1] AllowPublicReadAccessToAllObjects<br>[2] s3:GetObject

[tech]<br><br>Alternative to try catch for error handling?	"Result<T, E><img src=""1745620461329.jpg"">"
[JavaScript]<br><br>How to do Result(T,E) in pure JavaScript?	"// Conventionally called ""Result""<br>function ok(value) {<br>&nbsp; &nbsp; return { ok: true, value }; <br>&nbsp; &nbsp; // equivalent to Result(T, never)<br>}<br><br>function err(error) {<br>&nbsp; &nbsp; return { ok: false, error }; <br>&nbsp; &nbsp; // equivalent to Result(never, E)<br>}"
In pure JavaScript, how would you add docstrings for Result T,E ?	/**<br> * @template T<br> * @template E<br> * @typedef { { ok: true, value: T } | { ok: false, error: E } } Result<br> */
[JavaScript]<br><br>What is flatmap used for?	"When using map, sometimes the result will be nested. For example:<br><br>const result = map(parseJSON(jsonStr), getName);<br>// result = { ok: true, value: { ok: true, value: ""Luke"" } }<br>// BAD: it's a Result *inside* a Result<br><br>const result = flatMap(parseJSON(jsonStr), getName);<br>// result = { ok: true, value: ""Luke"" }"
"Rewrite the following using flatmap and Result<t,e> using pure JavaScript:<br><br><br><pre><code>async function fetchUser(id) {<br>  const res = await fetch(`/api/users/${id}`);<br>  if (!res.ok) throw new Error(`HTTP ${res.status}`);<br>  return res.json();<br>}<br><br>async function extractName(user) {<br>  if (user.name) return user.name;<br>  throw new Error(""Missing name"");<br>}<br><br>async function uppercase(str) {<br>  return str.toUpperCase();<br>}<br><br>async function main() {<br>  try {<br>    const user = await fetchUser(1);<br>    const name = await extractName(user);<br>    const upper = await uppercase(name);<br>    console.log(""Success:"", upper);<br>  } catch (e) {<br>    console.error(""Error:"", e.message);<br>  }<br>}<br><br>main();</code></pre></t,e>"	"<pre><code>
function ok(value) {<br>  return { ok: true, value };<br>}<br><br>function err(error) {<br>  return { ok: false, error };<br>}<br><br>async function flatMapAsync(result, fn) {<br>  return result.ok ? await fn(result.value) : result;<br>}<br><br>async function mapAsync(result, fn) {<br>  return result.ok ? ok(await fn(result.value)) : result;<br>}<br><br>// --------------------<br>// Async operations<br>// --------------------<br><br>async function fetchUser(id) {<br>  try {<br>    const res = await fetch(`/api/users/${id}`);<br>    if (!res.ok) return err(`HTTP ${res.status}`);<br>    const data = await res.json();<br>    return ok(data);<br>  } catch (e) {<br>    return err(`Network error: ${e.message}`);<br>  }<br>}<br><br>async function extractName(user) {<br>  return user.name ? ok(user.name) : err(""Missing name"");<br>}<br><br>async function uppercase(str) {<br>  return ok(str.toUpperCase());<br>}<br><br>// --------------------<br>// Main composed flow<br>// --------------------<br><br>async function main() {<br>  const result = await flatMapAsync(<br>    await fetchUser(1),<br>    user =&gt; flatMapAsync(<br>      extractName(user),<br>      name =&gt; uppercase(name)<br>    )<br>  );<br><br>  if (result.ok) {<br>    console.log(""Success:"", result.value);<br>  } else {<br>    console.error(""Error:"", result.error);<br>  }<br>}<br><br>main();
</code></pre>"
alternatives to git reset --hard (still using git reset)	git reset --soft<br>git reset --mixed
[git]<br><br>what do the following do?<br>git reset --soft<br>git reset --mixed	soft: Undo commit but keep changes in the staging area.<br><br>mixed: Undo commit, but keep files in the working directory. (This is the default when you do `git reset`)
"[git]<br><br>Here is the objective:&nbsp;<div><h3><b>Throw away all local changes (both tracked & untracked) and sync with remote</b></h3></div><br>Instead of the following:<br><br>git fetch origin<br>git reset --hard origin/main<br># destructive!<br><br>What is a safer alternative?"	"<b>0. git fetch origin</b><br><br><b>1. git reset --mixed origin/main</b><br>(move HEAD and current branch pointer to origin/main & reset staging area to match origin/main)<br><br><b>2. git restore .</b><br>(Discard local changes to tracked files in current dir and subdirs & reset them to HEAD)<br><br><b>3. git clean -nd</b><br># preview untracked files to delete from working directory <br><br><b>4. git clean -fd</b><br># delete untracked files/directories from working directory "
"[git]<br><br>Here is the objective:<br><br><div><h3><b>Undo a commit AND discard uncommitted changes in tracked files, and in working directory.""</b></h3></div><div>How do you do this without git reset --hard ?</div>"	"git reset --mixed HEAD~<br># rm commit, keep changes in the wd<br>&nbsp;<br>git restore .<br># discard changes in wd"
[git]<br><br>what does `git reset --soft &lt;COMMIT&gt;` do?	It moves the current branch (your HEAD) to another commit.<br>It moves the index to match that commit, but leaves the working directory unchanged.<br><br>Example:<br>git reset --soft HEAD~1<br>This undoes the last commit, but all changes from that commit will still be staged.

[bash]<br><br>Log stdout to tmp.log but ignore errors using exec &gt;	exec &gt; /tmp.log 2&gt; /dev/null
[bash]<br><br>exec > /dev/tty 2>&1<br><br>What is risky about this?	"Risk:<br><br>It assumes /dev/tty is the original stdout/stderr.<br><br>If its not (e.g., running from cron, script, or redirected context), this may fail or misroute output.<br><br><br>Safer alternative: Save and restore original file descriptors<br><br>exec 3>&1 4>&2         # Save original stdout (fd 1) and stderr (fd 2)<br>exec >> /tmp.log 2>&1  # Redirect stdout and stderr to a file<br><br># ... run commands ...<br><br>exec 1>&3 2>&4         # Restore original stdout and stderr<br><br>This approach doesn't assume anything about /dev/tty. It safely restores output streams regardless of environment."
What's the issue with this?<br><br>try {<br>     fetchUserData()<br>    } catch (error) {<br>    throw new Error(`Failed to fetch user data: ${error.message}`);<br>  }	In JavaScript anything can be thrown.<br><br>So we don't know if that's even an error. We don't know if it contains .message.<br><br>So what do we do?<br><br>We can check to make sure it's an error first using instanceof, or use Result<T,E>, or tuples in the form of [result, err]

[containers]<br><br><div>What Linux kernel features do containers rely on?</div>	"<div><div><ol><li><br><div> <b>Namespaces</b>  isolate process ID, network, filesystem, etc.</div><br></li><li><br><div> <b>Cgroups</b>  limit and account for resources (CPU, memory, etc.)</div><br></li><li><br><div> <b>OverlayFS/</b><b>UnionFS&nbsp;</b> layered filesystems for image composition</div></li><li><br><div> <b>Capabilities</b>  fine-grained control of root privileges</div><br></li><li><br><div> <b>User namespaces</b>  allow unprivileged users to act like root inside container</div><br></li></ol></div><br><div></div></div><div><h2><b>&nbsp;</b><b style=""font-size: 20px;"">&nbsp;5-Letter Mnemonic:&nbsp;</b></h2><div><h2><b>NUCOC</b></h2><h2><b>&nbsp;(pronounced like new-cock or nuke-ock if you want a cleaner image )<br></b></h2></div></div><div><div><h2><b> Mental Image to Remember NUCOC:</b></h2></div><br><blockquote>Imagine a <b>new container</b> (NUCOC) being born, and its wrapped in:</blockquote><br><div><ul><li><br><div>a <b>Namespace suit</b> (to stay isolated)</div><br></li><li><br><div>wearing <b>User privilege gloves</b> (to look like root, but isnt)</div><br></li><li><br><div>eating <b>Cgroup snacks</b> (carefully rationed CPU/memory)</div><br></li><li><br><div>standing on <b>Overlay blocks</b> (layered filesystems)</div><br></li><li><br><div>and protected by a <b>Capability shield</b> (so it cant nuke the host)</div><br></li></ul></div><br><div></div></div><div><br></div>"

What are escape sequences?	"<div>An <b>escape sequence</b> is a special string of characters used to <b>send instructions</b> to the terminal (or another system) that wouldnt be possible using normal text.</div>
<div><br></div>
<div>It starts with the <b>escape character</b>, which is ESC (represented as \033 or \x1b), followed by other characters that define the command.</div>
<div><br></div>
<div>Think of it like whispering a secret instruction to the terminal:</div>
<div><br></div>
<blockquote>Hey, dont show this as textdo something with it.</blockquote>"
Why do escape sequences exist?	"<div>Because terminals are basically just fancy text interpreters. But over time, they learned how to:</div>
<div><ul><li>
<div>move the cursor</div>
</li><li>
<div>change colors</div>
</li><li>
<div>clear the screen</div>
</li><li>
<div>rename tabs</div>
</li><li>
<div>set bold/underline</div></li></ul><div><div>All of that is controlled via <b>escape sequences</b>.</div></div></div><div><br></div><div><div><h3><b> Simple Examples</b></h3></div>
<div><b>1.&nbsp;</b><b>Newline</b></div></div><div><div>`echo -e ""Line 1\nLine 2""`</div></div><div><div>Here, \n is an escape sequence for a new line.</div></div><div><br></div><div><div><b>2.&nbsp;</b><b>Colors</b></div></div><div><b>`</b>echo -e ""\033[31mRed Text\033[0m""`</div><div><div><ul><li>
<div>\033[ = start an ANSI escape sequence</div>
</li><li>
<div>31m = red text</div>
</li><li>
<div>0m = reset to default</div></li></ul><div><div><b>3.&nbsp;</b><b>Move Cursor</b></div></div></div></div><div><b>`</b>echo -e ""\033[10A""`</div><div><div>Moves the cursor <b>up 10 lines</b>.</div></div><div><br></div>"

"The short head starts more lateral than the long head. It travels underneath the long head towards the femur and attaches near the linea aspera, lateral supracondylar line. <br><br>The long head starts a bit more medial and inferior, and travels up towards the ischial tuberosity, and sacrotuberous ligament over the short head.<br><br><br><img src=""biceps-femoris-lateral-long-and-short-heads.jpg.webp""><br><br><img src=""3_biceps_femoris_long_head-875x1024.png""><br><br><img src=""c09dc30816e6a98dde198d8245298109.jpg"">"
"[bash]<br><br>use lsof to get the ""current working directories"" of all of your processes"	<code>lsof -d cwd</code><br><br>(Lists the current working directories (cwd) of all open processes.)<br><br>Use sudo if you want to see processes owned by other users:<br><br><code>sudo lsof -d cwd</code><br><br><br>Note: lsof has many powerful options  consult the man page<br><br>
use lsof to get the <b>current working directories</b> of processes by:<br><br>1. name<br>2. pid	"<code>lsof -a -d cwd -c commandname<font face=""Arial""><br></font></code><code><font face=""Arial""><br></font>lsof -a -d cwd -p processid</code>&nbsp;<br><br>---<br><br>Commands:<br><br>lsof -a -d cwd -c commandname<br><br>Lists processes whose current working directory (cwd) is shown.<br><br>-c programname: filter by command name.<br><br>-d cwd: restrict to file descriptor of type cwd.<br><br>-a: AND all conditions (i.e., must match -c and -d).<br><br><br>Notes:<br><br>-a is essential here; without it, lsof would return results matching either -d cwd or -p/-c, which isnt what you want.<br><br>-d cwd zeroes in on the current working directory descriptor.<br><br>This is useful for finding what directory a process is ""in""."

[vscode] [devcontainers]<br><br>In a VSCode Dev Container, how can you avoid permission issues with node_modules without needing a chown in postCreateCommand?	"Avoid the permission issue by ensuring that the container always uses the correct user (like node) from the start.<br><br>How to fix it properly:<br><br>1. In your Dockerfile, set the final USER to node:<br><br>USER node<br><br>2. In your devcontainer.json, ensure the container runs as the same user:<br><br>""remoteUser"": ""node""<br><br>3. Also, avoid creating node_modules or running npm install as root during image build.<br><br>---<br><br>By aligning the build-time and runtime user, node_modules is always owned by the correct user (node), so no sudo chown is needed in postCreateCommand."

[bash]<br><br>What does -x option do in a script?<br>ie set -x	-x prints every command before executing, prefixed with a +
[Bash]<br><br>What does the -e option do in a script?<br><br>ie `set -e`	-e exit immediately if any command fails.<br><br>Otherwise it will keep running.<br><br>Historically, there were two philosophies for debugging: 1. As soon as the program encounters an error it should exit.<br>2. The program should keep running until the end, or until terminated.
[Bash]<br><br>In a bash script, what does the option -u do?<br><br>ie set -u	-u treat unset variables as errors.<br><br>If we try and access a variable that doesn't exist then it's an error.
[git]<br><br>What does this do?<br><br>git restore -WS .	Discards:<br><br> all uncommitted changes<br> And all staged files, <br><br>returning to the latest commit.
What does arn stand for?<br><br>As is arn:aws:s3?	Amazon resource name
"<br>In the story of the S3 Bucket Bouncer, who is the ""Principal""?<br>"	"The Principal is the person trying to get into the club (S3 bucket). It could be anyone (""*"") or a specific identity like a user or role. It answers the question: ""Who is the rule about?""<br><br> In AWS (and broader security contexts), the term ""principal"" comes from identity and access management (IAM) terminology. Its borrowed from security and law, where a principal is the primary party involved in an action or contract.<br><br>"
"What does the ""Effect"" represent in the S3 Bucket Bouncer analogy?"	"The Effect is the bouncers decision: Allow them in or Deny entry. Deny always overrides Allow. It answers the question: ""What does the rule do to the request?"""
"In the S3 Bucket Bouncer story, what does ""Action"" represent?"	"Action is what the person is trying to do at the club  get a drink, enter the VIP lounge, etc. In S3 terms, it's download, upload, delete, list, etc. It answers the question: ""What do they want to do?"""
"What is the ""Resource"" in the S3 Bucket Bouncer metaphor?"	"The Resource is the thing they want access to  the VIP room, bar, or dance floor. In AWS, its a bucket, folder, or file (identified by an ARN). It answers: ""What are they trying to access?"""
"Complete this sentence in the S3 Bucket Bouncer story:<br><br>""Let anyone [who] download [verb] to any file [noun], and we allow [ ] it."""	"""Let anyone (Principal) do (Action) to any file (Resource), and we Allow (effect) it."""
"What does ""Principal"": ""*"" mean in the S3 Bucket Bouncer story?"	It means everyone  including unauthenticated, anonymous people  can try to enter. The bouncer doesnt check ID.
"Why is ""Effect"": ""Deny"" stronger than ""Effect"": ""Allow"" in S3 policies?"	Because the bouncer has a rule: If theres ever a Deny rule, thats final. No other permission can override it.
[vim]<br><br>:%s/test1/test2/g<br><br>What does each part of this do in vim?	: enters command mode<br><br>% targets the entire file<br><br>s/test1/test2 means to substitute test1 with test 2<br><br>/g means to do it globally, rather than just the first occurrence <br>
[vim]<br><br>:s/foo/bar/g	Replace all occurrences of foo with bar, just on the current line.<br><br>(:s is shorthand for :.s)<br><br>In Vim, :.s is shorthand for:<br><br>:1,1s<br><br>Which means:<br>substitute (s) on the current line (.).<br><br>Breaking it down:<br><br>: starts a command<br><br>. refers to the current line<br><br>s is the substitute command<br><br><br>So :.s/foo/bar/g means:<br>Substitute all foo with bar on the current line.
[vim]<br><br>What does this do?<br><br>:10,20s/error/warning/g	Replaces all occurrences of error with warning from line 10 to line 20
[tech]<br>[vim]<br><br>What does this do?<br><br>:.,$s/old/new/g	"Replaces old with new from the current line until the end of the file.<br><br><br>In Vim, the comma in :.,$s/old/new/g separates the range of lines on which the substitution command should act.<br><br>Here's a breakdown:<br><br>.  the current line.<br><br>$  the last line of the file.<br><br>.,$  means ""from the current line to the end of the file"".<br><br><br>So:<br><br>:.,$s/old/new/g<br><br>says: ""Substitute 'old' with 'new' on every line from the current line (.) through the last line ($), globally on each line (g).""<br><br>The comma is the range separator between the starting and ending lines. "
[git]<br><br>git rm -r folder<br>vs<br>git rm -r --cached folder	git rm -r folder removes the folder from tracking and also removes it from your local working directory.<br><br>git rm -r --cached folder removes the folder from tracking, but doesnt remove the file from your local working directory.
What are git's 3 core layers?<br>+ 4th layer for collaboration?	1. Working directory (working tree)<br>2. Cache (index, or staging area)<br>3. Repository (where commit snapshots are stored)<br><br>4. Remote repository 
"Git:<br><br>What does the ""cache"" refer to?"	To the index/staging area.
[tech]<br><br>What is the escape sequence representation for the escape character?<br><br>+ What is the alternative?	\033 <br><br>\x1b
[tech]<br><br>\033[31m<br><br>What is this?	\033 is the escape sequence for the escape character <br><br>The following [ tells the terminal that what follows \033[ are commands to be run, not just stuff to be printed. (Known as the Control Sequence Introducer (CSI))<br><br>The trailing 'm' is specific to the Select Graphic Rendition (SGR), which deals with text formatting: color, weight, etc.<br><br>There are others besides 'm'.
[Emacs]<br><br>Delete from cursor to start of word	Alt-Del<br><br>(M-Del in Emacs notation)
What is git reset?<br><br>Is it:<br>A) git reset --soft<br>B) git reset --mixed<br>C) git reset --hard	git reset --mixed
[git]<br><br>What is git restore?	"It's used to undo changes in your working directory or staging area.<br><br>It's hard to remember because it doesn't seem to make sense.<br><br>But it's like telling git ""get me a clean copy from the repo or index and overwrite my current file.""<br><br>Examples:<br><br>git restore file.txt<br>Discard local changes to file.txt (reset it to last commit)<br><br>git restore --staged file.txt<br>Unstage file (move it from staged back to working directory without losing edits)<br><br>git restore --source=COMMIT_ID file.txt<br>Restore file.txt from a specific commit.<br><br>git restore .<br>Restores every file in the current directory and all subdirectories to their last committed state (HEAD).<br><br>git restore -WS<br>(shorthand for git restore --source=HEAD --worktree --staged .)"
Why might having a parasite reduce bile?	Because bile is bad for parasites. So many of them use mechanisms to try and reduce it in the host.
[bash]<br><br>What does this do?<br><br><pre><code>mkdir -p frontend/src/{components,hooks,utils,styles,pages,stores,types}</code></pre>	It creates multiple directories: frontend/src/components, frontend/src/hooks, etc.
You are writing the Value&lt;T,E&gt; stuff in pure javascript for error handling.<br><br>Write the ok() function.	"<pre><code>
function ok(value) {
  return { ok: true, value };
}
</code></pre>"
You are writing the Value&lt;T,E&gt; stuff in pure javascript for error handling.<br><br>Write the err() function.	"<pre><code>
function err(error) {
  return { ok: false, error };
}
</code></pre>"
You are writing the Value&lt;T,E&gt; stuff in pure javscript..<br><br>Write the map function (async).	"<pre><code>

async function mapAsync(result, fn) {
  return result.ok ? ok(await fn(result.value)) : result;
}

</code></pre>"
You are writing the Value&lt;T,E&gt; stuff in pure javscript..<br><br>Write the flat map function (async).	"<pre><code>

async function flatMapAsync(result, fn) {
  return result.ok ? await fn(result.value) : result;
}

</code></pre>"

<script>
  // remove cloze syntax from revealed hint
  var hint = document.querySelector('.fullhint>[id^=""hint""]')
  var html = hint.innerHTML.replace(/\[\[oc(\d+)::(.*?)(::(.*?))?\]\]/mg, ""$2"")
  hint.innerHTML = html
  // scroll to cloze
  document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function() {
    setTimeout(function(){
      const cloze1 = document.getElementsByClassName(""cloze"")[0];
      const rect = cloze1.getBoundingClientRect();
      const absTop = rect.top + window.pageYOffset;
      const absBot = rect.bottom + window.pageYOffset;
      if (absBot >= window.innerHeight) {
        const height = rect.top - rect.bottom
        const middle = absTop - (window.innerHeight/2) - (height/2);
        window.scrollTo(0, middle);};
    }, 1);
  }, false);
</script>

[git]<br><br>When to use `git add -A`?	git add -A is a combination of the following:<br>1) git add .&nbsp; (stages new and modified files in the current dir and subdirs)<br>2) git add -u&nbsp; (stages modifications and deletions for tracked files)
[git]<br><br>`git add -A` is a combination of 2 git commands.&nbsp;<br>What are they?	git add -u<br>&amp;&amp; git add .
[git]<br><br>git restore<br>vs<br>git reset	git restore affects the working directory.<br>It's used to discard uncommitted changes in your files.<br><br>git reset affects the staging area and/or commit history.<br>It is used to move pointers (branches, HEAD), and optionally modify staged or working files.
[git]<br><br>Difference between git restore -W and git restore -S	"<table><tbody><tr><th>
<div><b>Command</b></div>
</th><th>
<div><b>Effect</b></div>
</th></tr><tr><td>
<div>git restore --staged file</div>
</td><td>
<div>Unstages the file (keeps changes in working dir)</div>
</td></tr><tr><td>
<div>git restore --worktree file or -W</div>
</td><td>
<div>Discards changes in working dir (keeps staged)</div>
</td></tr><tr><td>
<div>git restore --staged --worktree file or -SW</div>
</td><td>
<div>Restores file to last commit (unstages &amp; discards changes)</div></td></tr></tbody></table>"
"[vscode]<br><br><img src=""CleanShot 2025-05-01 at 16.56.44@2x.png""><br><br>The top used to just say ""viscera"". To get it to show the following what do I do?"	In settings, search for window.title.<br><br>Bonus: Then you can set it to something like ${activeEditorShort}${separator}${folderPath}
[bash]<br><br>Fix this command:<br>fd -g '_ai/**/llm-merge_master'	fd -g '**/llm-merge_master' _ai
[bash]<br><br>How do these 3 fd command variations work?<br><br>1. fd -g '_ai' Dev<br><br>2. fd -g '*_ai*' Dev<br><br>3.&nbsp;fd -gp '**/_ai' Dev	"1. Looks in Dev folder for glob pattern '_ai'. In this case it finds it.<br><br>2. Looks in Dev folder for glob pattern '*_ai*'. It finds a lot of things that contain the substring ""ai"", such as&nbsp;/pytz/zoneinfo/America/Argentina/Buenos_Aires.<br><br>3. Looks in Dev folder for glob pattern '**/_ai', using -p flag, which tells it to use the pattern for the whole path. So it looks for and finds&nbsp;Dev/_ai/ successfully, as intended."
[git]<br><br>Which command messes with the commit history?<br><br>git restore<br><br>git reset	git reset 
<div>What does the --loader flag do in Node.js?</div>	<div>&nbsp;It allows you to manually specify a custom module loader, such as Yarns .pnp.loader.mjs for ESM projects using PlugnPlay.</div>
<div>What is .pnp.loader.mjs used for in a Yarn PlugnPlay project?</div>	<div>&nbsp;It is Yarns custom ESM loader that enables Node.js to resolve modules according to PnP rules.</div>
[yarn]<br><br>Why might using <br><b>mocha --loader .pnp.loader.mjs</b> <br>directly fail in a yarn PnP project?	Running Mocha directly does not fully initialize the Yarn PnP environment, even with the loader specified. <br><br>This can lead to subtle module resolution failures, such as packages not being found or incorrectly resolved.<br><br><u>Recommended fix</u>:<br><b>yarn (dlx) mocha --loader .pnp.loader.mjs</b>
<div>What happens if you run yarn mocha --loader .pnp.loader.mjs in a Yarn PnP project?</div>	<div>&nbsp;It can cause a conflict because Yarn already sets up the PnP loader, and adding the --loader flag redundantly re-applies it, potentially causing errors like ERR_METHOD_NOT_IMPLEMENTED.</div>
[yarn]<br><br><div>Why is running yarn mocha (without --loader) the correct way in a Yarn PnP environment?</div>	<div>Because Yarn automatically sets up the PnP environment and loader, allowing Mocha to work correctly without needing an explicit --loader flag.</div>
[yarn]<br><br><div>When is it appropriate to use the --loader .pnp.loader.mjs flag manually?</div>	<div>Only when you run a Node.js script directly <i>outside</i> of Yarn (ie not using `yarn mocha ...`), and you need to manually tell Node to use Yarns PnP loader.</div>
<div>Whats the core problem with mixing Yarn and manual --loader flags?</div>	<div>&nbsp;It creates conflicting module resolution logic by trying to apply the PnP loader twice, leading to runtime errors or unexpected behavior.</div>
[git]<br><br>Delete all uncommitted files and directories.	git clean -fd. (f stands for force, d for directories)<br>
[git]<br><br>What is a detached HEAD state?	You are no longer working on a branch.<br><br>Instead, you are directly viewing or modifying a specific commit.
[git]<br><br>Tell me about this command:<br><br>git switch --detach origin/main	This is the same as:<br><br>git switch origin/main, since it's a remote branch it will be detached anyways.
[nodejs]<br><br>Fields inside of package.json:<br><br><table><tbody><tr><th><br><div><b>Field</b></div><br></th><th><br><div><b>Purpose</b></div><br></th></tr><tr><td><br><div>main</div><br></td><td><br><div><br></div><br></td></tr><tr><td><br><div>module</div></td><td><br></td></tr><tr><td><br><div>exports</div></td><td><br></td></tr><tr><td><br><div>types</div><br></td><td><br><div><br></div></td></tr></tbody></table>	<table><tbody><tr><th><div><b>Field</b></div></th><th><div><b>Purpose</b></div></th></tr><tr><td><div>main</div></td><td><div>Default entry point for CommonJS (require())</div></td></tr><tr><td><div>module</div></td><td><div>Entry point for ES modules (used by bundlers like Rollup, Webpack)</div></td></tr><tr><td><div>exports</div></td><td><div>Explicitly define imports/exports for different environments/formats</div></td></tr><tr><td><div>types</div></td><td><div>Entry point for TypeScript definitions</div></td></tr></tbody></table>
[tech]<br>[git]<br><br>Scenario:&nbsp;<br><br>I created a repo, which lives inside of viscera/.<br><br>Outside of that folder, I have descriptions/ and other files. I also turned that into a git repo as well.<br><br>I accidentally did `git add .` in the outer repo, and it added everything in viscera/ as well. I haven't made any commits or pushes yet.<br><br>How do I remove viscera/ from the staging area?	"<div>[WRONG]</div><div><h3><b>&nbsp;</b><b style=""font-size: 20px;"">git restore --staged viscera</b></h3></div><div><div>fatal: could not resolve HEAD</div></div><div><br></div><div><br><div><div> <b>Why This Happens</b><b></b></div><br><div>git restore --staged relies on HEAD (the latest commit) to know what to restore to.</div><br><div>If there are <b>no commits yet</b>, Git has no reference point  so the command fails.</div></div></div><div><br></div><div>[CORRECT]</div><div><div><h3><b>&nbsp;</b><b style=""font-size: 20px;"">git reset viscera</b></h3></div><br><div><ul><li><br><div>Unstages viscera</div><br></li><li><br><div> <b>Does NOT delete files from working directory.</b><b></b></div><br></li><li><br><div> <b>If viscera was already committed then git will still track it.</b><b></b></div><br></li><li><br><div>No change to git commit history.</div></li></ul></div></div><div><br></div><div>[CORRECT]</div><div><div><h3><b>&nbsp;</b><b style=""font-size: 20px;"">git rm --cached -r viscera</b></h3></div><div><ul><li><br><div> <b>Keeps all files on disk. Does NOT delete files fom working directory.</b><b></b></div><br></li><li><br><div> Git marks it for <b>deletion from the repo on the next commit.</b><b></b></div><br></li><li><br><div> Use when you want to:</div><br><div><ul><li><br><div>Stop tracking a folder</div><br></li><li><br><div>Add it to .gitignore afterward</div></li></ul></div></li></ul></div></div><div><b><br></b></div><div><h3><b>&nbsp;</b><b style=""font-size: 20px;"">git rm -r viscera</b><b style=""font-size: 20px;"">&nbsp;( Dangerous)</b></h3></div><div><br><div><ul><li><br><div><div><ul><li><br><div><b>Deletes the viscera folder from disk</b><b></b></div><br></li><li><br><div>Removes it from Git <i>and</i> your filesystem</div><br></li><li><br><div>Only use if you want to permanently delete it</div></li></ul></div></div></li></ul></div></div><div><br></div>"
[git]<br><br>Remove a file from the staging area, and tell git to delete it from the repo on the next commit.	git rm --cached &lt;file&gt;<br><br>Note: it's history will still exist, so in past commits the file/folder will still be there.
[git]<br><br>Remove a file from the staging directory, but keep it in the working directory.<br><br>If it's already being tracked then keep tracking it.<br><br>In other words: Dont commit this change yet, but still track this file in the future.	git restore --staged &lt;file&gt;
[yarn]<br><br><div><b>How to tell the Yarn (v2/3/4) interpreter that this is the root of a Yarn project?</b><b></b></div><div><b><br></b></div>ie. if it keeps looking up the directory tree for where the project root is.<br>	Add an empty yarn.lock or .yarnrc.yml file into the project root directory.
"[esbuild]<br><br><div>What does `""bundle"": true` do in esbuild?</div>"	"It tells esbuild to follow all `import` and `require` statements and include **all dependent modules** (including local files and packages from `node_modules`) into a single bundled output file.<div><br></div><div><div><b>Why? </b>Without `""bundle"": true`, esbuild expects external files (like `./controlScript/cleanStringForObjectExtraction.js`) to be present on disk at runtime  so missing modules cause errors.&nbsp;</div></div><div>(Hence, me getting this error <i>Cannot find module `./controlScript/cleanStringForObjectExtraction.js`)</i></div><div><i><br></i></div><div><u>Note</u><i>:&nbsp;</i>With ""bundle"": false (the default), esbuild treats your file like a Node.js script  it just transpiles it but leaves imports unresolved.</div>"
"[podman] [buildah]<br><br>Difference between the concept of a ""container"" in buildah vs podman?"	"<div>In <b>Buildah</b>, containers are <b>ephemeral, build-time constructs</b>. Theyre not meant to be long-lived or executed in the traditional sense. Instead, they exist to allow <b>modifying and assembling container images</b>, similar to RUN instructions in a Dockerfile.</div>
<div><br></div>
<div>In <b>Podman</b>, containers are <b>runtime containers</b>, intended to <b>run services or processes</b>, potentially long-lived  just like containers in Docker.</div><br>`buildah run` command emulates the RUN command in a Dockerfile<br>`podman run` command emulated the `docker run` command functionality.<br><br>* You cannot see Podman containers from within Buildah.&nbsp;<br>&nbsp; And you cannot see Buldah containers from within Podman.<br><div><ul><li>
<div>Thats because:</div>
<div><ul><li>
<div>Buildah uses its own <b>storage and metadata</b> for build containers.</div>
</li><li>
<div>Podman uses <b>libpod</b> for container lifecycle and runtime management.</div>
</li></ul></div></li></ul></div>"
[containers]<br><br>Can you use colima with podman?	"<div><br>  Despite the presence of the --runtime podman flag in Colima, its <b>non-functional</b> and has been <b>deprecated/ignored</b>.<br></div><br><div></div><br><div><br>  <div><h3><b> TL;DR:</b></h3></div><br>  <blockquote><b>Colima only supports Docker runtime.</b></blockquote><br>  <blockquote><b>Podman must be run via its own podman machine VM on macOS.</b></blockquote><br>  <blockquote><b> Why?</b></blockquote><br>  <blockquote><br>    <div><br>      <ul><br>        <li><div><b>Colima</b> uses <a href=""https://github.com/lima-vm/lima"">Lima</a> under the hood, which technically <i>can</i> run Podman.</div></li><br>        <li><br>          <div>However, Colima developers <b>never completed full Podman support</b>, due to:</div><br>          <div><br>            <ul><br>              <li><div>Lack of stable, cross-platform tooling</div></li><br>              <li><div>Compatibility issues with volumes, networking, and DNS on macOS</div></li><br>            </ul><br>          </div><br>        </li><br>        <li><div>Thats why <code>colima start --runtime podman</code> shows:</div><br>          <blockquote>unsupported container runtime 'podman'</blockquote><br>        </li><br>      </ul><br>    </div><br>  </blockquote><br><br>  <div><h3><b> What to Do Instead</b></h3></div><br>  <div>Use <b>Podmans native VM for macOS.</b></div><br>  <div><br>    <div>This works <b>independently of Colima</b> and gives you:</div><br>    <div><br>      <ul><br>        <li><div>Rootless containers</div></li><br>        <li><div>Docker-compatible CLI</div></li><br>        <li><div>Integration with Buildah and Skopeo</div></li><br>      </ul><br>    </div><br>  </div><br><br>  <div><h3><b> What If I Still Want to Use Colima?</b></h3></div><br>  <div><br>    <p><b> Stick with Colima + Docker:</b> This is the only stable and officially supported configuration. It integrates well with Docker CLI, Compose, and most development tools on macOS.</p><br>    <p><b> Workarounds (not recommended or officially supported):</b></p><br>    <ul><br>      <li><br>        <b>Manual Lima + Podman setup:</b> You can bypass Colima and configure Lima manually using the <a href=""https://github.com/lima-vm/lima/blob/master/examples/podman.yaml"">Podman example template</a>. However, you'll lose Colima's CLI conveniences.<br>      </li><br>      <li><br>        <b>Use Podman CLI with Docker alias:</b> Install Podman via Homebrew, start its VM with <code>podman machine init/start</code>, and optionally alias <code>docker=podman</code>. This allows partial Docker CLI compatibility but may break Compose and volume usage.<br>      </li><br>    </ul><br>  </div><br></div>"
[colima] [podman]<br><br>On MacOS why do you need to choose beetween podman and colima?	"<div><h3><b> They each manage their own virtual machine and container ecosystem.</b></h3></div><div><img src=""CleanShot 2025-05-06 at 12.47.15@2x.png""></div><div><div><h3><b> Why you&nbsp;</b><b style=""font-size: 20px;"">cant mix them</b></h3></div>
<div><ul><li>
<div>Colima and Podman <b>dont share containers, images, or networks</b>.</div>
</li><li>
<div>Each runs in its own <b>isolated Linux VM</b>.</div>
</li><li>
<div>Only <b>one VM can be active on your system at a time</b> (for performance, port conflicts, etc.).</div></li></ul></div></div>"
[linux]<br><br>What is CRIU?	"""Checkpoint Restore In Userspace""<br><br><div><b>CRIU</b> allows you to <b>freeze a running Linux process</b>, save it to disk, and <b>resume it later</b>, even on another machine.</div><br><div><ul><li><br><div>Think of it like <b>pause and save</b> for containers or processes.</div><br></li><li><br><div>Originally built for high-performance computing (HPC), now used in some container runtimes.</div></li></ul><div><div><h3><b> Key Use Cases:</b></h3></div><br><div><ul><li><br><div>Live migration of containers (move a running container to another host)</div><br></li><li><br><div>Fast startup by restoring pre-warmed containers</div><br></li><li><br><div>Process snapshotting in debugging or fault tolerance</div></li></ul><div><div><div><h3><b> How It Works with Containers:</b></h3></div><br><div><ul><li><br><div>Tools like <b>Podman</b>, <b>LXC</b>, and <b>containerd</b> can integrate CRIU for container checkpoint/restore</div></li></ul><div>Example:</div><div>podman container checkpoint my-container<br>podman container restore my-container<br></div></div></div><br><div><h3><b> Limitations:</b></h3></div><br><div><ul><li><br><div>Only works on <b>Linux</b> with <b>kernel support</b><b></b></div><br></li><li><br><div>Doesnt support all container features (e.g., GPUs, some mounts)</div><br></li><li><br><div>Complex to set up; rarely used in general DevOps workflows</div></li></ul></div></div></div></div></div>"
[containers]<br><br>What is CRI-O?	"Cree Runs In Open <br><br>""Container Runtime Interface - Open""<br><br>- it's not Linux-based<br>- it's kubernetes-based<br><br><div><b>CRI-O</b> is a lightweight, production-ready container runtime that implements the <b>Kubernetes Container Runtime Interface (CRI)</b> and uses <b>OCI-compliant containers</b> (Open Container Initiative).</div><br><div><ul><li><br><div>Its built to <b>replace Docker in Kubernetes clusters</b><b></b></div><br></li><li><br><div>Designed to <b>run containers</b> without the Docker daemon</div></li></ul></div><br><div><h3><b> Architecture:</b></h3></div><br><div><ul><li><br><div>CRI-O plugs into Kubernetes via the <b>CRI API</b><b></b></div><br></li><li><br><div>Internally uses:</div><br><div><ul><li><br><div><b>runc</b> to run containers</div><br></li><li><br><div><b>conmon</b> to manage logs and container lifecycle</div><br></li><li><br><div><b>image and storage libraries</b> shared with Podman/Buildah</div></li></ul></div></li></ul></div><div><div><h3><b> Benefits:</b></h3></div><br><div><ul><li><br><div>Lightweight alternative to Docker in Kubernetes</div><br></li><li><br><div>Fewer moving parts = better performance and security</div><br></li><li><br><div>Shared codebase with Podman and Buildah</div><br></li></ul></div><br><div><br></div><br><div><h3><b> What Its&nbsp;</b><b style=""font-size: 20px;"">Not</b></h3></div><br><div><ul><li><br><div>Not a CLI tool  it runs as a system service under Kubernetes</div><br></li><li><br><div>Not useful outside Kubernetes environments</div><br></li></ul></div><br><div></div></div>"
[git]<br><br>git reset:<br><br>- soft vs mixed vs hard<br><br>- how to use git reset?	<table><tbody><tr><th><br><div><b>Command</b></div><br></th><th><br><div><b>What it does</b></div><br></th><th><br><div><b>Affects</b></div><br></th><th><br><div><b>Typical Use Case</b></div><br></th></tr><tr><td><br><div>git reset --soft &lt;commit&gt;</div><br></td><td><br><div>Move HEAD to the specified commit. Keep changes <b>staged</b>.</div><br></td><td><br><div>HEAD Index Working Dir</div><br></td><td><br><div>Keep your code and staging, just rewind the commit</div><br></td></tr><tr><td><br><div>git reset --mixed &lt;commit&gt; (default)</div><br></td><td><br><div>Move HEAD and unstage the changes. Keep them in the working directory.</div><br></td><td><br><div>HEAD Index (cleared) Working Dir</div><br></td><td><br><div>Want to unstage files but keep your changes</div><br></td></tr><tr><td><br><div>git reset --hard &lt;commit&gt;</div><br></td><td><br><div>Move HEAD and <b>erase everything</b> back to the specified commit.</div><br></td><td><br><div>HEAD Index Working Dir</div><br></td><td><br><div>Revert everything  use with caution</div></td></tr></tbody></table>

What is one of the main advantages of duckdb?	It can query data without having to ingest it. <br><br><br>To elaborate: DuckDB can run SQL queries directly on external files like Parquet, CSV, and others without loading them into a separate internal database format. <br><br>This is especially useful for:<br> - Exploratory data analysis<br> - Ad hoc querying of large datasets<br> - Lightweight ETL tasks<br><br>This behavior is similar to how SQLite operates, but optimized for analytical workloads (OLAP) rather than transactional workloads.
[git]<br><br>1. What does `git clean` do?<br>2. What are some common git clean examples?	"It is used to remove untracked files and directories from your working directory.<br><br>This helps you clean up files that are not being tracked by Git (i.e. files not added with git add), such as build artifacts, temporary files, or generated logs.<br><br><b><u>Common Usage</u></b><br><br><b>git clean -n:</b><br>Dry run  shows what would be deleted without actually deleting anything.<br><br><b>git clean -f:</b><br>Force  actually deletes the untracked files.<br><br><b>git clean -fd:</b><br>Deletes untracked files and directories.<br><br><b>git clean -fx:</b><br>Deletes untracked files including files ignored by .gitignore.<br><br><b>git clean -fdx:</b><br>Deletes untracked files and directories including ignored ones.<br><br>---<br><br><b><u>Examples</u></b><br><br># Preview what will be deleted<br>git clean -n<br><br># Remove untracked files<br>git clean -f<br><br># Remove untracked files and directories<br>git clean -fd<br><br># Remove all untracked files, including ignored ones<br>git clean -fdx<br><br>Warning: git clean is permanent. It doesnt move files to the trash  theyre gone unless you have a backup. Always use -n first to see what will be deleted.<br><br>"
[pkg management]<br><br>Difference between compatible release specifier (~=) and the caret specifier (^)?	"They both define version ranges in dependency management  but they are used in different ecosystems and follow different rules.<br><br>---<br><br>1. Compatible release specifier (~=)  Python / PEP 440<br><br>Used in Python (e.g. in requirements.txt, pyproject.toml):<br><br>package ~= 1.4 translates to:<br>>=1.4.0 and <2.0.0<br><br>~= 1.4.2<br>means:<br>>=1.4.2 and <1.5.0<br><br>---<br><br>2. Caret specifier (^)  JavaScript / Rust / Cargo / Node (npm)<br><br>""^1.4.2""<br>translates to:<br>>=1.4.2 and <2.0.0<br><br>But:<br><br>^0.3.4  >=0.3.4 and <0.4.0 (because 0 is special  considered unstable)<br><br>^0.0.3  >=0.0.3 and <0.0.4<br><br>---<br><br>TL;DR<br><br>~= (Python): pins all digits to the left of the last one you specify.<br><br>^ (JavaScript/Rust): pins the leftmost non-zero digit."
[git]<br><br>What is the difference between git clean and git restore?	<b>git restore</b><br><br>Restores modified tracked files to the last commit.<br><br>Does not touch untracked or ignored files.<br><br>Think of it as: Undo changes to files Git is already tracking.<br><br><b>git clean</b><br><br>Deletes untracked files and directories.<br><br>Useful for getting rid of leftover files (like compiled binaries, temp files, etc).<br><br>Think of it as: Clean up things Git doesnt know about.<br>
[git]<br><br>When would you use both git restore and git clean?	Typical used together<br><br>If you want to reset everything in your working directory (like a clean slate):<br><br>git restore .<br>git clean -fd<br><br>This combination:<br><br>Discards all changes to tracked files.<br><br>Deletes all untracked files and folders.
[git]<br><br>Discard all changes to tracked files.<br><br>Delete all untracked files and folders.	git restore .<br>git clean -fd
[git] what git command can be used to check why a directory or file is being ignored?	git check-ignore -v path/to/directory
