<div>[math]<br></div><div><br></div><div><b>Why is</b></div>\(|\vec{a} \times \vec{b}| = |\vec{a}| \cdot |\vec{b}| \cdot \sin(\theta)\)<br><br><div><div><div><b>What does this represent geometrically?</b></div></div></div>	"<div>This equation expresses the <b>magnitude of the cross product</b>, which equals the <b>area of the parallelogram</b> formed by vectors <b>a</b> and <b>b</b>.</div><br><div><ul><li><div>\(|\vec{a}|\)&nbsp;is the length of vector <b>a</b> (the base).</div></li></ul></div><br><div><ul><li><div><span style=""white-space: pre;"">\(|\vec{b}| \cdot \sin(\theta)\)</span>&nbsp;is the&nbsp;<b>height</b>&nbsp; the component of&nbsp;<b>b</b>&nbsp;thats&nbsp;<b>perpendicular</b>&nbsp;to&nbsp;<b>a</b>.</div></li></ul></div><div><br></div><br><div>So the area is:&nbsp;</div><div>\(\text{Area} = \text{base} \cdot \text{height} = |\vec{a}| \cdot |\vec{b}| \cdot \sin(\theta)\)</div><div></div><div><br></div><div>This matches the <b>magnitude of the cross product</b>:</div><br><div><ul><li><br><div><b>Zero</b> if the vectors are parallel (&nbsp;\(\sin(\theta) = 0\)&nbsp;)</div><br></li><li><br><div><b>Maximum</b> if they are perpendicular (&nbsp;\(\sin(\theta) = 1\))</div><br></li></ul><div><br></div></div><div><img src=""cross_product_parallelogram.png""><br></div><br><div></div><img src=""IMG_20250519_172241.jpg"">"
[math]<br><br>Difference between dot-product and cross-product?	"<img src=""Visual Representation of Cross Product a  b = Area.png""><br><div>&lt;p style=""font-size: 0.8em; color: gray; margin-top: 4px;""&gt;</div><div>This diagram shows how the dot product of two vectors is calculated geometrically:&nbsp;Red: Vector a,&nbsp;Green: Vector b,&nbsp;Blue: The projection of b onto a,&nbsp;Dashed line: The perpendicular dropped from b to a.</div><div>&lt;/p&gt;</div><div><br></div><b>dot-product</b> is a scalar of how much 2 vectors both point the the same direction.<br>This number will be highest when the 2 vectors point in the exact same direction. If they are perpendicular then the result will be 0.<br><br><br>
<img src=""Visual Representation of Dot Product a  b.png""><br><br><b>cross-product&nbsp;</b>is represented by a new vector that is perpendicular to both input vectors.&nbsp;Its magnitude equals the area of the parallelogram formed by the two vectors:&nbsp;\(\vec{a}\)&nbsp;&amp;&nbsp;\(\vec{b}\)"
self-similarity vs autocorrelation	"[math]<br><br><b>self-similarity</b>&nbsp;is a mathematical property where an object looks the same or very similar to itself as it is scaled up or down.<br><br>If self-similarity is analogous to <i>temperature</i>&nbsp;then&nbsp;<b>autocorrelation</b>&nbsp;is analgous to the <i>thermometer</i>.<br>It's a way of measuring self-similarity.<br><br>

<img src=""Autocorrelation of Sine Wave.png""><br><p>This image shows an example using a sine wave. If we take the sine wave and <b>shift it horizontally</b>, then <b>compare it to the original sine wave</b> at each shift, we can generate a graph called the <b>autocorrelation</b>.</p><div><p>In this graph:</p>
<div><ul><li>
<p>A value of <b>+1</b> means the shifted sine wave <b>aligns perfectly</b> with the original (theyre in phase).</p></li><li><p>A value of <b>-1</b> means the shifted sine wave is the <b>exact opposite</b> of the original (theyre out of phase by 180, or  radians).</p></li><li>
<p>Values in between reflect <b>partial similarity</b>.</p></li></ul></div>
<p>This shows the <b>self-similarity</b> of the sine wave over different time shifts.</p></div>"
Break this down into programming lessons:	"<div><a href=""file:///Users/luketych/Downloads/cascading_complexity_audit.md"">file:///Users/luketych/Downloads/cascading_complexity_audit.md</a><a href=""file:///Users/luketych/Downloads/cascading_complexity_audit.md"">file:///Users/luketych/Downloads/cascading_complexity_audit.md</a>""Want a real example? Even the creator of htop, Hisham Muhammad, later wrote about wishing hed had better UI primitives to build it in a more robust, maintainable way.""</div><div><br></div><div>Tell me more..<br><br><br><div>Absolutely  this is a real and insightful story.</div><div><br></div><div><h3><b> The Story: Hisham Muhammad and&nbsp;</b></h3><h3><b>htop</b></h3></div><div><br></div><div><b>Hisham Muhammad</b>&nbsp;is the original creator of&nbsp;<a href=""https://htop.dev/""><b>htop</b></a>&nbsp; the popular interactive process viewer for Unix systems. Its one of the most beloved TUIs ever made, used globally by sysadmins and developers.</div><div><br></div><div>But despite its popularity,&nbsp;<b>Hisham later reflected critically</b>&nbsp;on his experience maintaining and extending htop.</div><div></div><div><h3><b> What He Said (Summary of His Reflections)</b></h3></div><div><br></div><div>In a&nbsp;<a href=""https://hisham.hm/2016/09/02/a-farewell-to-htop/"">2016 blog post titled&nbsp;<i>A farewell to htop</i></a>&nbsp; when he stepped away from the project  Hisham shared several frustrations:</div><div><br></div><div><b> 1.&nbsp;</b><b>Poor Modularity and Maintainability</b></div><div><br></div><blockquote>htop was a monolith, hard to extend and hard to modify.</blockquote><div><br></div><div>He originally wrote it as a C program with ncurses, without anticipating its future complexity. As features grew, the codebase became harder to work with.</div><div><br></div><div><b> 2.&nbsp;</b><b>Tight Coupling with the Terminal</b></div><div><br></div><blockquote>Theres only so far you can go with ncurses before things get hacky.</blockquote><div><br></div><div>He described the complexity of updating views, dealing with refreshes, and redrawing  all made harder by the&nbsp;<b>inherent limitations of the terminal</b>.</div><div><br></div><div><b> 3.&nbsp;</b><b>Technical Debt Due to Terminal Constraints</b></div><div><br></div><div>He mentioned how&nbsp;<b>even simple UI changes required wrestling with escape sequences, resizing issues</b>, and various terminal inconsistencies.</div><div></div><div><h3><b> Notable Quote:</b></h3></div><div><br></div><blockquote>I often fantasized about rewriting htop in a different architecture, with proper model/view separation, and maybe even writing a graphical version.</blockquote><div><br></div><div>This shows that even one of the most successful terminal-based tools was held back by the&nbsp;<b>terminal itself</b>.</div><div></div><div><h3><b> So Why Did He Stick With TUI?</b></h3></div><div><br></div><div>Because when htop was born (circa 2004), TUIs were still the&nbsp;<b>only portable way</b>&nbsp;to create rich-ish UIs on headless or minimal systems.</div><div></div><div><h2><b> Key Takeaway</b></h2></div><div><br></div><div>Even the creator of one of the&nbsp;<b>best TUIs ever made</b>&nbsp;wishes hed built it with&nbsp;<b>more flexible UI primitives</b>&nbsp; ideally, something that separated:</div><div><ul><li><div><b>data and model logic</b><b></b></div></li><li><div><b>rendering and view logic</b><b></b></div></li><li><div><b>input handling</b></div></li></ul></div><div><br></div><div>This is exactly the kind of thing that GUI toolkits or canvas-based engines (like SDL or LVE) allow today.</div><div></div><div>Would you like a breakdown of how htop would look if reimagined as a GUI app using minimal pixels or a framework like ImGui?<br><br></div></div><div><br></div><div><div>tell me about ncurses, and also tell me about how the complexity grew as the project scaled</div></div><div><br></div><div><br></div><div><br></div><div><div>Absolutely. Lets break this into two parts:</div><div></div><div><h2><b> 1. What is&nbsp;</b></h2><h2><b>ncurses</b></h2><h2><b>?</b></h2></div><div><br></div><div><h3><b> Summary:</b></h3></div><div><br></div><div><b>ncurses</b>&nbsp;is a C library for building text-based user interfaces in the&nbsp;<b>terminal</b>. It provides functions to move the cursor, change colors, draw boxes, handle keyboard input, etc.  without manually sending raw ANSI escape codes.</div><div><br></div><div>It was created to abstract over inconsistencies in terminal capabilities.</div><div></div><div><h3><b> Key Features of&nbsp;</b><b>ncurses</b></h3><h3><table><tbody><tr><th><div><b>Feature</b></div></th><th><div><b>What it does</b></div></th></tr><tr><td><div><b>Windowing system</b></div></td><td><div>Allows multiple text windows or regions</div></td></tr><tr><td><div><b>Cursor movement</b></div></td><td><div>Move the cursor to arbitrary positions on the screen</div></td></tr><tr><td><div><b>Color support</b></div></td><td><div>Use colors, bold, reverse video, etc.</div></td></tr><tr><td><div><b>Keyboard input</b></div></td><td><div>Detect keypresses (arrow keys, function keys, etc.)</div></td></tr><tr><td><div><b>Screen redrawing</b></div></td><td><div>Automatically refresh only parts of the screen that changed</div></td></tr><tr><td><div><b>Terminal capability database</b>&nbsp;(terminfo)</div></td><td><div>Makes apps work across many different terminal types</div></td></tr></tbody></table></h3></div></div><div><b><br></b></div><div><b><br></b></div><div><b><br></b></div><div><div><h3><b> What Its Good For:</b></h3></div><div><ul><li><div>Lightweight dashboards and monitoring tools (e.g. htop, tig, vtop)</div></li><li><div>Full-screen terminal apps</div></li><li><div>Cross-platform TUI development</div></li></ul></div><div></div><div><h3><b> What Its Bad At:</b></h3></div><div><ul><li><div><b>Pixel-level control</b>&nbsp;(cant draw graphics)</div></li><li><div><b>Layout precision</b>&nbsp;(limited by monospace grid)</div></li><li><div><b>Input consistency</b>&nbsp;(Backspace, Esc, etc. vary by terminal)</div></li><li><div><b>Modern UX needs</b>&nbsp;(scrolling, drag/drop, animations)</div></li></ul></div><div></div><div><h2><b> 2. Why Complexity Explodes in&nbsp;</b></h2><h2><b>ncurses</b></h2><h2><b>&nbsp;Projects (like&nbsp;</b></h2><h2><b>htop</b></h2><h2><b>)</b></h2></div><div><br></div><div><h3><b> 1.&nbsp;</b></h3><h3><b>No Real Layout System</b></h3></div><div><ul><li><div>Everything is built on&nbsp;<b>absolute positioning</b>&nbsp;(move(y, x)).</div></li><li><div>You must manually calculate dimensions, alignment, overflow, etc.</div></li><li><div>Imagine trying to&nbsp;<b>resize and reflow multiple UI panels</b>&nbsp;in a resizable terminal manually.</div></li></ul></div><div><br></div><div><h3><b> 2.&nbsp;</b></h3><h3><b>Terminal Quirks Multiply</b></h3></div><div><ul><li><div>Backspace might emit ^H or ^?</div></li><li><div>Escape key delays input (conflicts with arrow key sequences)</div></li><li><div>Some keys are&nbsp;<b>undetectable</b>&nbsp;(e.g. Ctrl+Shift+arrow)</div></li></ul></div><div><br></div><div>This leads to&nbsp;<b>tons of if/else branches and hacks</b>&nbsp;just to interpret keyboard input.</div><div><br></div><div><h3><b> 3.&nbsp;</b></h3><h3><b>Rendering Is State-Dependent</b></h3></div><div><ul><li><div>You must&nbsp;<b>keep track of the full screen state</b>&nbsp;to redraw only whats changed (refresh()).</div></li><li><div>Forgetting to wrefresh() or drawing in the wrong window = flickering or ghost UI.</div></li></ul></div><div><br></div><div><h3><b> 4.&nbsp;</b></h3><h3><b>No Separation of Logic and UI</b></h3></div><div><ul><li><div>In many ncurses apps, the&nbsp;<b>business logic is tangled with drawing code</b>.</div></li><li><div>That makes testing, refactoring, and maintaining it hard as features are added.</div></li></ul></div><div><br></div><div><h3><b> 5.&nbsp;</b></h3><h3><b>Handling Concurrency or Live Updates</b></h3></div><div><ul><li><div>Terminal rendering isnt thread-safe by default.</div></li><li><div>So updating e.g. CPU usage and handling input at the same time? You need careful mutexes or event loops.</div></li></ul></div><div><br></div><div><h3><b> 6.&nbsp;</b></h3><h3><b>Internationalization (i18n) is a Nightmare</b></h3></div><div><ul><li><div>Unicode rendering with wide characters, double-width Asian characters, RTL scripts  all require&nbsp;<b>manual hacks</b>&nbsp;in ncurses.</div></li></ul></div><div></div><div><h2><b> In&nbsp;</b></h2><h2><b>htop</b></h2><h2><b>&nbsp;Specifically:</b></h2></div><div><br></div><div>As features grew (like tree view, search, filters, per-core CPU meters), the team had to:</div><div><ul><li><div><b>Manually manage multiple windows and redraw regions</b><b></b></div></li><li><div>Handle&nbsp;<b>weird bugs in terminal emulators</b><b></b></div></li><li><div>Tangle&nbsp;<b>input handling</b>&nbsp;with&nbsp;<b>UI rendering</b><b></b></div></li><li><div>Add&nbsp;<b>custom code</b>&nbsp;to support colors, bold text, line-drawing characters</div></li></ul></div><div><br></div><div>Eventually, the codebase became harder to reason about, which Hisham (the original author) admitted in his farewell post.</div><div></div><div><h2><b> TL;DR</b></h2></div></div><div><table><tbody><tr><th><div><b> Feature</b></div></th><th><div><b> ncurses Strength</b></div></th><th><div><b> Pain Point as Project Scales</b></div></th></tr><tr><td><div>Initial layout &amp; input</div></td><td><div>Easy</div></td><td><div>Hard to maintain as UI grows</div></td></tr><tr><td><div>Portability</div></td><td><div>Great</div></td><td><div>Terminal quirks creep in</div></td></tr><tr><td><div>Rendering model</div></td><td><div>Simple</div></td><td><div>Gets fragile with animations</div></td></tr><tr><td><div>Modularity &amp; testing</div></td><td><div>None</div></td><td><div>Everything is stateful</div></td></tr><tr><td><div>Unicode &amp; accessibility</div></td><td><div>Not built-in</div></td><td><div>Requires extra effort</div></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div><b><br></b></div><div><b><br></b></div><div><b><br></b></div><div><div><br></div><div>If youre building complex or dynamic interfaces, consider:</div><div><ul><li><div><b>ImGui</b>&nbsp;(for modern GUI with minimal overhead)</div></li><li><div><b>LVE / SDL / SFML</b>&nbsp;(canvas-based rendering)</div></li><li><div><b>React + Tauri</b>&nbsp;(if going cross-platform GUI)</div></li><li><div>Even&nbsp;<b>CLI tools with web dashboards</b>&nbsp;(e.g. using Textualize or Rich to bridge CLI and HTML)</div></li></ul></div><div></div><div>Want a working code comparison between ncurses and something like Dear ImGui to show how much less pain the modern approach involves?</div></div><div><br></div><div><div><br></div><div><br></div><div>what lessons can we abstract out of this example that would help a programmer to know more about cascading and compounding complexities and uncertainties?</div></div><div><br></div><div><br></div><div><br></div><div><br></div><div><div>This is a powerful question  because what youre really asking is:</div><div><br></div><blockquote><b>How do small, manageable systems become fragile monsters  and how can we see it coming before its too late?</b><b></b></blockquote><div><br></div><div>Using htop + ncurses as the case study, here are&nbsp;<b>key lessons and abstracted patterns</b>&nbsp;about&nbsp;<b>cascading complexity and compounding uncertainty</b>&nbsp;that apply to any growing software project.</div><div></div><div><h2><b> 1.&nbsp;</b></h2><h2><b>Early Optimizations Create Long-Term Lock-In</b></h2></div><div><ul><li><div>Hisham picked ncurses because it let him get a working UI&nbsp;<b>quickly</b>.</div></li><li><div>But it&nbsp;<b>locked the project</b>&nbsp;into escape sequences, fixed-width grids, and termcap quirks.</div></li><li><div><b>Lesson:</b>&nbsp;The path of least resistance today becomes the concrete slab you cant dig under tomorrow.</div></li></ul></div><div><br></div><blockquote> Beware when a dependency that solves&nbsp;<i>everything</i>&nbsp;at first starts to dictate your architecture.</blockquote><div></div><div><h2><b> 2.&nbsp;</b></h2><h2><b>Tight Coupling + Lack of Separation = Scaling Pain</b></h2></div><div><ul><li><div>htop grew organically  logic and UI were tangled.</div></li><li><div>As complexity increased (tree views, filters, metrics), small UI changes required deep refactors.</div></li><li><div><b>Lesson:</b>&nbsp;Early disregard for separation of concerns leads to fragile interdependencies.</div></li></ul></div><div><br></div><blockquote> Ask early:&nbsp;<i>If I had to replace this whole UI or engine, could I do it without rewriting the logic?</i><i></i></blockquote><div></div><div><h2><b> 3.&nbsp;</b></h2><h2><b>Local Workarounds Become Global Hazards</b></h2></div><div><ul><li><div>The Backspace workaround (ctrl-h) solved one issue.</div></li><li><div>But it reveals a broader truth:&nbsp;<b>Terminal I/O is not standardized</b>, and your workaround for one emulator breaks another.</div></li><li><div><b>Lesson:</b>&nbsp;Fixes that solve one edge case often introduce hidden branches of future failure.</div></li></ul></div><div><br></div><blockquote> Be suspicious of hacks that fix symptoms without solving root causes  they accumulate entropy.</blockquote><div></div><div><h2><b> 4.&nbsp;</b></h2><h2><b>Low-Level Control Becomes a Liability</b></h2></div><div><ul><li><div>With ncurses, you control every redraw, every input event, every position  great for precision.</div></li><li><div>But every feature adds&nbsp;<b>state</b>, and now youre managing dozens of tiny decisions at once.</div></li><li><div><b>Lesson:</b>&nbsp;Micro-control scales poorly unless wrapped in modular abstractions.</div></li></ul></div><div><br></div><blockquote> Use libraries that give you&nbsp;<b>high-level primitives</b>&nbsp;when youre solving high-level problems.</blockquote><div></div><div><h2><b> 5.&nbsp;</b></h2><h2><b>Growing Surface Area = Exponential Uncertainty</b></h2></div><div><ul><li><div>Supporting more platforms, terminals, key layouts, screen sizes introduces&nbsp;<b>nonlinear complexity</b>.</div></li><li><div>Tiny features create&nbsp;<b>interactions</b>&nbsp;you cant predict.</div></li><li><div><b>Lesson:</b>&nbsp;Complexity isnt additive  its&nbsp;<b>combinatorial</b>.</div></li></ul></div><div><br></div><blockquote> Ask:&nbsp;<i>How many things does this new feature depend on? How many things depend on it?</i><i></i></blockquote><div></div><div><h2><b> 6.&nbsp;</b></h2><h2><b>If It Wasnt Built to Evolve, It Cant</b></h2></div><div><ul><li><div>htop wasnt modular. It wasnt built for plug-ins, rendering engines, or layout changes.</div></li><li><div>Once usage scaled,&nbsp;<b>refactoring was too risky</b>, so it ossified.</div></li><li><div><b>Lesson:</b>&nbsp;Code that isnt designed for evolution will rot under pressure.</div></li></ul></div><div><br></div><blockquote> Favor simplicity, but plan for change  even when you think youll never need it.</blockquote><div></div><div><h2><b> 7.&nbsp;</b></h2><h2><b>The Medium Shapes the System</b></h2></div><div><ul><li><div>The&nbsp;<b>terminal</b>&nbsp;was the root cause of many of htops growing pains  fixed-width grids, limited input models, platform inconsistencies.</div></li><li><div>Even though Hisham wrote great code, the&nbsp;<b>environment constrained what was possible</b>.</div></li><li><div><b>Lesson:</b>&nbsp;The platform you choose early on shapes what your software can become.</div></li></ul></div><div><br></div><blockquote> Choose your foundation based not on what works&nbsp;<i>today</i>, but whats composable&nbsp;<i>tomorrow</i>.</blockquote><div></div><div><h2><b> Abstracted Pattern:&nbsp;</b></h2><h2><b>Entropy Traps</b></h2></div><div><br></div><blockquote>A project starts simple. You layer in features.</blockquote><blockquote>Then: each new thing requires&nbsp;<b>more exception handling, more special-cases, more glue code</b>.</blockquote><blockquote>Eventually, the glue becomes so heavy you cant move.</blockquote><div><br></div><div><b>The trap is thinking that complexity will scale linearly. It never does.</b><b></b></div><div></div><div><h2><b> Tools to Recognize and Prevent This</b></h2></div></div><div><table><tbody><tr><th><div><b>Tool / Habit</b></div></th><th><div><b>How it helps</b></div></th></tr><tr><td><div> Separation of concerns</div></td><td><div>Decouples UI, logic, rendering, input</div></td></tr><tr><td><div> Testability</div></td><td><div>Forces clearer modular design</div></td></tr><tr><td><div> Layered abstraction</div></td><td><div>Allows platform swaps without deep rewrites</div></td></tr><tr><td><div> Complexity audits</div></td><td><div>Ask: How many modules talk to this one?</div></td></tr><tr><td><div> Domain boundaries</div></td><td><div>Design systems as&nbsp;<b>composable blocks</b>, not patches</div></td></tr><tr><td><div> Resist easy now, hard later</div></td><td><div>Optimize for&nbsp;<b>changeability</b>, not just speed</div></td></tr></tbody></table><br></div><div><br></div><div><br></div><div>#  Cascading Complexity Audit Worksheet<br><br>&gt; Run this for a project, feature, or module.&nbsp; <br>&gt; Score each question from 03:<br>&gt; - 0 = No concern&nbsp; <br>&gt; - 1 = Minor concern&nbsp; <br>&gt; - 2 = Noticeable friction&nbsp; <br>&gt; - 3 = Clear source of risk / tech debt<br><br>---<br><br>##  Modularity &amp; Separation<br><br>| Question&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; | Score |<br>|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|-------|<br>| Is UI logic separated from business/data logic?&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; |&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; |<br>| Can rendering/output be swapped (e.g. terminal to GUI) without rewriting core logic?&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; |&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; |<br>| Can you test logic **without** launching the full app or environment?&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; |&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; |<br><br>---<br><br>##  Composability &amp; Changeability<br><br>| Question&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; | Score |<br>|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|-------|<br>| Can you add a new feature without modifying more than 2 files/modules?&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; |&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; |<br>| Can you remove a feature without cascading changes elsewhere?&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; |&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; |<br>| Are components **composable** (can they be reused in a different order or context)?&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; |&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; |<br><br>---<br><br>##  Abstractions vs. Escape Hatches<br><br>| Question&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; | Score |<br>|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|-------|<br>| Are you relying on low-level details (e.g. ANSI escape codes, byte streams)?&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; |&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; |<br>| Are there ""special cases"" hardcoded into otherwise reusable code?&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; |&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; |<br>| Are you re-implementing things your platform should abstract for you?&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; |&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; |<br><br>---<br><br>##  Platform &amp; Environment Lock-In<br><br>| Question&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; | Score |<br>|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|-------|<br>| Is your system tied to a platform with known inconsistencies (e.g. terminals)?&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; "[physio]<br><br>Describe ""form closure"" vs ""force closure"""	<b>Form Closure</b> describes stability provided by the shape and geometry and fit of the bones (and also ligaments.)<br>Form closure is often found in deep, stable joints.<br><br><b>Force Closure</b>&nbsp;describes stability provided by the muscular forces, fascia, and connective tissues that compree and stabilize the joint.

How many ligaments attach to the coccyx?	6
[anatomy]<br><br>Muscles that attach to the coccyx?	Coccygeus<br>Levator Ani group:<br>  iliococcygeus<br>  pubococcygeus<br>Gluteus maximus (deep fibers)<br>External anal sphincter (via fascia)
<div>What connects the perineal body to the coccyx?</div>	The anococcygeal ligament (raphe), which acts as a fascial midline tether from the coccyx to the perineal body.
<div>What is the difference between the filum terminale internum and externum?</div>	<div>Internum: inside the dural sac (L2S2).</div><div>Externum: outside the dural sac, attaches the dural sac to the coccyx (S2Co1).</div>
<div>What is the filum terminale externum and how can it affect the coccyx?</div>	Its a fibrous extension of the spinal cord dura mater that attaches to the coccyx. <br>It stabilizes the cord. <br>If overly taut (e.g., in tethered cord syndrome), it can exert upward (cephalad) pull on the coccyx.
[anatomy]<br><br><div>Which muscles converge at the perineal body?</div>	<b>p</b>ubococcygeus, <br><b>b</b>ulbospongiosus, <br><b>s</b>uperficial transverse perineal muscles, <br><b>d</b>eep transverse perineal muscles<br><b>e</b>xternal anal sphincter.<br><br>mnemonic:<br><blockquote><b>People Buy Super Delicious Eggs</b><b></b></blockquote><br>
<div>[anatomy]</div><div><br></div><div>What is the perineal body and how does it affect the coccyx?</div>	The perineal body is a fibromuscular node at the center of the perineum. <br>It connects multiple pelvic floor muscles and the anococcygeal ligament. <br>Asymmetry in its tension can pull on the coccyx and shift it from midline.
[anatomy]<br><br><div>Which muscles blend with the thoracolumbar fascia and influence coccyx alignment?</div>	Gluteus maximus, <br>latissimus dorsi, <br>erector spinae, <br>hamstrings (via the sacrotuberous ligament)
[anatomy]<br><br><div>What is the deep posterior (thoracolumbar) fascia and how does it relate to the coccyx?</div>	Its a multi-layered fascial sheath connecting the spine, sacrum, and glutes. It transmits load and tension through the sacrotuberous ligament, which anchors to the coccyx  thus indirectly influencing coccyx position and stability.
[anatomy]<br><br><div>How can fascial asymmetry in the pelvic floor lead to coccyx deviation?</div>	If one side of the fascia is tighter, it can pull the coccyx laterally through tension on the pelvic floor muscles and ligaments, especially the anococcygeal ligament.
[anatomy]<br><br><div>What major muscles does the pelvic floor fascia envelop that attach to the coccyx?</div>	Levator ani group (iliococcygeus and pubococcygeus), <br>coccygeus,<br>external anal sphincter.
[anatomy]<br><br><div>What is the pelvic floor fascia and how does it affect the coccyx?</div>	The pelvic floor fascia (endopelvic fascia) is a sheet of connective tissue enveloping pelvic organs and muscles. <br>It attaches to the coccyx and transmits muscular and fascial tension. <br>Asymmetry in this fascia can pull the coccyx off midline or increase tension on one side.

[data science]<br><br>CatBoost uses ordered boosting to prevent target leakage.<br><br>1. What is ordered boosting?<br><br><br>2. How does it prevent target leakage	1. Ordered Boosting is a training technique where, instead of using the entire dataset at once, CatBoost simulates online learning by training each new data point using only the data points that came before it. This is done using permutations of the dataset and averaging the results to reduce variance.<br><br><br>2. It prevents target leakage by ensuring that the prediction for a given data point is not influenced by its own target label or by data points that come after it in the permutation. This mimics a real-world scenario where future information is unavailable, thereby avoiding information leakage that can lead to overly optimistic model performance.
[data science]<br><br>Why is CatBoost more resistant to overfitting on small datasets?	CatBoost is more resistant to overfitting on small datasets due to:<br><br>1. Ordered Boosting  Prevents target leakage by ensuring that each model is trained only on past data in a randomized order, avoiding using future labels.<br><br><br>2. Built-in Regularization  Incorporates techniques like L2 regularization and shrinkage (learning rate) to reduce model complexity.<br><br><br>3. Efficient Categorical Feature Handling  Uses target statistics without target leakage by applying permutations and Bayesian averaging, avoiding overfitting to noise in categorical data.<br><br><br>4. Oblivious Trees  Uses symmetric decision trees (same split across each level), which limits model flexibility and reduces the chance of over fitting compared to asymmetric trees.
[data science]<br><br>CatBoost handles categorical features natively.<br><br>What does this mean, and why is it an advantage?	CatBoost can process categorical features directly without requiring manual preprocessing like one-hot encoding or label encoding. It uses techniques such as target statistics and ordered permutations to convert categories into numerical representations during training.<br><br>Why its an advantage:<br><br>1. No manual preprocessing needed  Saves time and reduces human error.<br><br><br>2. Avoids overfitting  By using ordered target statistics, it prevents target leakage.<br><br><br>3. More efficient  Uses memory and compute more effectively than one-hot encoding, especially with high-cardinality features.<br><br><br>4. Better performance  Often leads to improved model accuracy compared to generic encoding methods.

"[physio]<br><br>What is ""hyperinflation""?"	"Hyperinflation is a state where (either unilateral or bilateral) the lungs remain <b>chronically expanded with air</b>, even during exhalation.<br><br>(Especially the <b>upper, anterior (front), and apical</b> regions)<br><br><br><div>The brainstem (specifically the <b>medulla oblongata</b>) monitors <b>CO levels</b>, not O, as the primary signal to breathe. When you over-breathe:</div>
<div><ul><li>
<div>CO drops too fast</div>
</li><li>
<div>Blood becomes more alkaline</div>
</li><li>
<div>The body compensates by <b>tightening airways, increasing tone</b>, and <b>limiting blood flow to regulate pH</b></div>
</li></ul></div>
<div><br></div>
<div>This is a form of <b>chemical stress</b>.</div>"

[data science]<br><br>What are odds? What is probability	<b>odds</b><br>The ratio of something happening : that thing not happening.<br>e.g. my team winning / my team not winning<br><br><b>probability</b><br>The ratio of something happening : every other possibility<br>e.g. my team winning / my team winning &amp; not winning
[data science]<br><br>What are the 2 ways of calculating odds?	1. From counts.<br>2. From probabilities.<br><br>ie If your team won 5 games and didn't win 3:<br><br><b>Using counts:&nbsp;</b><br>Odds = 5/3 = 0.625<br><br><b>Using probabilities:<br></b>Probability of winning = 5/8<br>Probability of not winning = 3/8<br>Odds = (5/8)/(3/8) = 5/3 = 0.625

[data science]<br><br>When using something like XGBoost for classification, why do we use log(odds)?	When determining where to split the tree, we have to add the resulting residuals of each model together.<br><br>But we can't add probabilities together because they would increase past 1.<br><br>So instead, we use log odds.

"<blockquote>[tech] [git]</blockquote><blockquote>In Git, the command git push origin :feature-backup is used to <span class=""cloze"" data-cloze=""delete&#x20;the&#x20;remote&#x20;branch&#x20;named&#x20;feature&#x2D;backup"" data-ordinal=""1"">[...]</span>.</blockquote>
<blockquote>This is functionally equivalent to <span class=""cloze-inactive"" data-ordinal=""2"">git push origin --delete feature-backup</span>.</blockquote>"	"<blockquote>[tech] [git]</blockquote><blockquote>In Git, the command git push origin :feature-backup is used to <span class=""cloze"" data-ordinal=""1"">delete the remote branch named feature-backup</span>.</blockquote>
<blockquote>This is functionally equivalent to <span class=""cloze-inactive"" data-ordinal=""2"">git push origin --delete feature-backup</span>.</blockquote><br>
<div><ul><li>
<div>The : means push nothing to that branch.</div>
</li><li>
<div>This command <b>does not delete the local branch</b>.</div>
</li><li>
<div>To delete a <b>local</b> branch:</div>
<div><ul><li>
<div>git branch -d feature-backup  safe (only if merged)</div>
</li><li>
<div>git branch -D feature-backup  force delete</div>
</li></ul></div></li></ul></div>"
"<blockquote>[tech] [git]</blockquote><blockquote>In Git, the command git push origin :feature-backup is used to <span class=""cloze-inactive"" data-ordinal=""1"">delete the remote branch named feature-backup</span>.</blockquote>
<blockquote>This is functionally equivalent to <span class=""cloze"" data-cloze=""git&#x20;push&#x20;origin&#x20;&#x2D;&#x2D;delete&#x20;feature&#x2D;backup"" data-ordinal=""2"">[...]</span>.</blockquote>"	"<blockquote>[tech] [git]</blockquote><blockquote>In Git, the command git push origin :feature-backup is used to <span class=""cloze-inactive"" data-ordinal=""1"">delete the remote branch named feature-backup</span>.</blockquote>
<blockquote>This is functionally equivalent to <span class=""cloze"" data-ordinal=""2"">git push origin --delete feature-backup</span>.</blockquote><br>
<div><ul><li>
<div>The : means push nothing to that branch.</div>
</li><li>
<div>This command <b>does not delete the local branch</b>.</div>
</li><li>
<div>To delete a <b>local</b> branch:</div>

"[tech] [git]<br><br>How to show what file-level hanges would occur if you checked out &lt;branch_name&gt;?<br><br>For example:<br><br><img src=""CleanShot 2025-06-20 at 17.47.35@2x.png"">"	git diff --name-status &lt;branch_name&gt;
[git]<br><br>Difference between these 2?<br><br>git diff --name-status refactor..HEAD<br>git diff --name-status HEAD..refactor	The first shows the files added, deleted, modifed in order to go from &lt;b&gt;refactor&lt;/b&gt; to &lt;b&gt;HEAD&lt;/b&gt;.<br><br>The second shows the files added, deleted, modified in order to go from &lt;b&gt;HEAD&lt;/b&gt; to &lt;b&gt;refactor&lt;/b&gt;.
[tech] [git]<br><br>What does the following mean?<br><br>&gt; git merge refactor<br>Already up to date.	The current branch already includes all commits that branch:refactor has in Git's history.
[tech] [git]<br><br>&gt; git merge refactor<br>Already up to date.<br><br>&gt; git diff refactor<br>&lt;b&gt;=&lt;/b&gt;&lt;i&gt;What do you expect here?&lt;/i&gt;	"It might still show differences.<br><br>It's a common mistake to think that because `git merge refactor` returns ""Already up to date"" that there are no file diffs.<br><br>""Already up to date"" means that the current branch already includes all &lt;b&gt;commits&lt;/b&gt; that branch:refactor has in Git's history.<br><br>&lt;b&gt;Git's merge check is based on commit history.&lt;/b&gt;<br><br>So even if branch:refactor has a new file if that file was already merged earlier via another branch (ie branch:feature-backup), which has since been merged into branch:main, then git considers branch:refactor already merged."
[tech] [git]<br><br>True or False?<br><br>Git looks at file differences when checking if a branch is up to date.	False.<br><br>Git only uses the commit ancestry.&nbsp;
"[tech] [git]<br><br>Scenario:<br><br>You want markdown_file.md to exist in your current branch, but `git merge &lt;other_branch&gt;` returns ""Already up to date.""<br><br>1) What is happening?<br>2) How do you get markdown_file.md into your current branch?"	1) `git merge &lt;other_branch&gt;` checks and concludes that all of the commits from git's history for other_branch are already in the current branch. &lt;b&gt;git merge&lt;/b&gt; does not care about file differences. That is a common misconception.<br><br>2) git checkout &lt;other_branch&gt; -- markdown_file.md<br><br>(This will copy that file into your current branch from the other_branch, w/o switching branches or merging.)

[tech]<br><br>su postgres <br>Vs<br>su - postgres	<b>su postgres</b><br> Keeps the current directory and most environment variables (like PATH, HOME) from the original user. It does not simulate a login, so it may not load the 'postgres' user's shell configuration files, like ~/.bash_profile.<br><br><b>su - postgres</b><br>Simulates a login shell, changing to the 'postgres' user's home directory (usually /var/lib/postgres) and setting environment variables based on the 'postgres' user's configuration, ensuring the correct setup for PostgreSQL tasks.

[tech]<br>[terminal]<br><br>What input events are terminals typically unable to detect?	Terminals usually cannot detect key-up and key-down events, only key presses.
[tech]<br>[terminal]<br><br>Can terminals detect key chords (multiple keys simultaneously)?	Not reliably.
[tech]<br>[terminal]<br><br>Why do terminals often confuse TAB with Ctrl+I?	Many terminals send the same ASCII code (0x09) for both, making them indistinguishable.
[tech]<br>[terminal]<br><br>Are modifier keys (shift, Ctrl, Alt, etc) reliable in the terminal?	No.<br><br>Especially when combined with other keys.<br><br><br>Modifier keys like Ctrl, Shift, and Alt modify other key inputs but terminals handle them inconsistently. <br><br>Ctrl is usually recognized, Shift often changes letter case, and Alt can send ambiguous escape sequences. <br><br>Terminals use varying, non-standard escape codes to report modifiers, often failing to detect multiple modifiers simultaneously. <br><br>This inconsistency causes bugs and limits shortcut support, especially in remote shells or multiplexers. <br><br>Newer terminals improve support, but handling modifiers remains a common challenge in terminal UI development.<br>
[tech]<br>[terminal]<br><br>What 2 limitations (in regards to terminal input) makes it very complicated for building advanced TUIs?	Can't detect keyup/keydown events.<br>Can't detect multiple simultaneous keys.
